# Validator Take

Validator take is the share of delegated-stake emissions that a validator keeps before the remaining
emissions flow to stakers
([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
[Emission: Distribution](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/emissions#distribution)).

The term is a distribution concept. It describes a split inside delegated-stake emissions after the
validator-side amount already exists, not the consensus step that produced that amount
([Yuma Consensus: Validator emissions](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/yuma-consensus#validator-emissions)).

## What It Represents

Validator take concerns the portion of emissions tied to delegated stake on a selected subnet. On
netuid 1, the key relationship is between a validator and the stakers who delegated to it: the take
is the validator's kept share, and the remaining delegated-stake emissions flow to those stakers at
tempo distribution ([Delegation](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/staking-and-delegation/delegation),
[Glossary: Tempo](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#tempo),
[Emission: Distribution](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/emissions#distribution)).

Examples tied to netuid 1 illustrate one subnet's commission split. They should not be read as
representing production settings on another network
([Bittensor Networks](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/concepts/bittensor-networks)).

## Distinction from Subnet Owner Take

On a subnet such as netuid 1, validator take and subnet owner take name different emission slices.
Validator take is the percentage a validator keeps from delegated-stake dividends before the
remainder flows to nominators, while subnet owner take is the documented 18 percent share of subnet
alpha emissions routed to the subnet owner as stake
([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
[Emission](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/emissions),
[Emission: Distribution](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/emissions#distribution)).

- **Validator take** — validator–delegator split on validation dividends at tempo distribution.
- **Subnet owner take** — global owner cut from that subnet's emission bucket.

## Distinction from Child Hotkeys

Validator take names the commission rate on validation dividends on a subnet such as netuid 1, while
a child hotkey names the authorized key a parent delegate uses to perform validation with
re-delegated stake
([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
[Child Hotkeys](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/validators/child-hotkeys)).

- **Validator take** — fee applied when dividends split between validator and stakers.
- **Child hotkey** — worker identity that earns dividends under delegation.

## Distinction from Dividends

Validator take is the share of validator dividends kept by the validator hotkey. Dividends are the
validator-side reward stream produced from subnet emissions before that split
([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
[Glossary: Dividends](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#emission)).

- **Dividends** — validator-side payout category consensus produces.
- **Validator take** — configured share kept from the delegated-stake portion at distribution.

## Distinction from Childkey Take

A child hotkey carries its own take rate, the [[Childkey Take]], which applies at a different point
in the dividend flow. Validator take is the commission a validator keeps from emissions tied to
delegated stake before the remainder reaches delegators
([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
[Child Hotkeys](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/validators/child-hotkeys)).

- **Validator take** — split between validator and its delegators.
- **[[Childkey Take]]** — split between parent hotkey and child hotkey validating on its behalf.

## Distinction from Validator Permit

Validator take is the commission on delegated-stake dividends. A validator permit is the on-chain
right to submit counting weights and take part in consensus
([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
[Glossary: Validator Permit](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-permit)).

- **Validator permit** — right to submit counting weights before dividends exist.
- **Validator take** — commission applied once delegated-stake dividends are credited.

## Distinction from Effective Stake

Effective stake is the combined staking total behind a delegate hotkey. Validator take is the
commission rate applied when delegated-emission returns are split at distribution
([Glossary: Effective Stake](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#effective-stake),
[Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-)).

- **Effective stake** — combined staking total behind a delegate hotkey.
- **Validator take** — commission rate on delegated returns at distribution.

## Distinction from Nominator

A nominator delegates TAO to a validator hotkey. Validator take names what share of
delegated-emission returns the validator keeps before the remainder flows to those nominators
([Glossary: Nominator](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#nominator),
[Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-)).

- **Nominator** — role that supplies delegated support.
- **Validator take** — configured share the validator keeps before the remainder flows to stakers.

## Distinction from Delegation Rewards

Validator take is the commission a validator keeps from delegated-emission returns before nominators
receive the remainder, while delegation rewards are what remains for delegated stake after that
split
([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
[Staking and delegation overview](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/staking-and-delegation/delegation)).

- **Validator take** — cut taken off the top of delegated returns.
- **Delegation rewards** — portion that reaches nominators afterward.

## Distinction from Emission Split

Validator take is not a fourth headline share in the emission split. It is the cut a validator keeps
from delegated stake inside the validator-and-staker bucket after that bucket is credited
([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
[Emission: Distribution](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/emissions#distribution)).

- **Emission split** — role proportions credited at tempo end.
- **Validator take** — commission applied inside the validator-and-staker bucket.

## Distinction from Incentives

[Incentives](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#incentives) name miner-side emission
outcomes produced from clipped and aggregated weight signals. Validator take names the configured
share a validator keeps when the delegated-stake portion is later split
([Yuma Consensus](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/yuma-consensus)).

- **Incentives** — miner-side emission outcomes from consensus.
- **Validator take** — validator commission on delegated-stake dividends at distribution.

## Distinction from Yuma Consensus

Validator take is the configurable commission a validator keeps from delegated-stake emissions at
distribution. It names a post-settlement split rule inside the staking relationship, not the
consensus mechanism that builds validator dividend shares from weight submissions
([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
[Delegation](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/staking-and-delegation/delegation)).

Yuma Consensus is the on-chain mechanism that runs at the epoch boundary on the selected netuid. It
reads the weight matrix from eligible validators, applies clipping and bonding, and converts the
result into miner incentives and validator dividend shares
([Yuma Consensus](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/yuma-consensus),
[Emission](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/emissions)).

Yuma produces the validator-side dividend pool from consensus; validator take applies afterward when
the delegated-stake portion is split between validator and nominators. Settlement and commission are
separate stages on the same emission path
([Yuma Consensus: Validator emissions](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/yuma-consensus#validator-emissions),
[Emission: Distribution](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/emissions#distribution)).

Readers should not read a higher take percentage as proof of stronger weight influence—that is stake
weight vocabulary. Take only governs how delegated dividends are shared after Yuma settles.

- **Validator take** — commission on delegated-stake validator emissions at distribution.
- **Yuma Consensus** — epoch-boundary settlement from validator weights to emission shares.

## Distinction from Staking

Validator take belongs to the staking relationship between a validator and the stakers who support
that validator. Delegation describes the support relationship, while validator take describes the
validator-kept share of the delegated-stake emissions
([Delegation](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/staking-and-delegation/delegation),
[Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-)).

- **Delegate stake / effective stake** — stake context around a validator.
- **Validator take** — how the delegated-stake emission share is split at distribution.

## Reader Boundary

Validator take should be read as reference vocabulary for emission distribution. It is not a
recommendation, validator quality score, or complete explanation of staking outcomes
([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
[Yuma Consensus: Validator emissions](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/yuma-consensus#validator-emissions)).

## Distinction from Delegate

Validator take and delegate name a fee and the party that charges it. A delegate is a validator that
accepts stake from nominators and validates on their behalf, while validator take is the percentage
that delegate keeps from the rewards generated on delegated stake before the remainder is paid to
nominators
([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
[Glossary: Delegate](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#delegate),
[Delegation](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/staking-and-delegation/delegation)).

- **Delegate** — a validator that accepts stake from nominators.
- **Validator take** — the commission that delegate keeps from delegated-stake rewards.

## Further Reading

- [Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-)
- [Emission: Distribution](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/emissions#distribution)
- [Yuma Consensus: Validator emissions](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/yuma-consensus#validator-emissions)
- [Delegation](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/staking-and-delegation/delegation)

content/pages/moving_stake/index.mdx:138:## Distinction from Conviction and Locked Stake
content/pages/moving_stake/index.mdx:140:Moving stake and conviction both act on an existing staked position, but they describe different
content/pages/moving_stake/index.mdx:141:things. Moving stake relocates a staked position between hotkeys and/or subnets in a single atomic
content/pages/moving_stake/index.mdx:142:transaction. Conviction and locked stake describe locking subnet alpha so it builds a time-based
content/pages/moving_stake/index.mdx:143:commitment score and the staked balance cannot be silently reduced below the locked amount
content/pages/moving_stake/index.mdx:144:([Staking and delegation overview: Moving stake](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/staking-and-delegation/delegation#moving-stake),
content/pages/moving_stake/index.mdx:145:[Conviction and locked stake](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/staking-and-delegation/conviction-staking)).
content/pages/moving_stake/index.mdx:147:Moving stake answers how a position is relocated; conviction answers whether part of a position has
content/pages/moving_stake/index.mdx:148:been locked for commitment. A conviction lock can constrain how much of a position moving stake
content/pages/moving_stake/index.mdx:149:could take out of that subnet.
content/pages/moving_stake/index.mdx:151:- **Moving stake** — relocation of delegated stake between hotkeys or subnets.
content/pages/moving_stake/index.mdx:152:- **Conviction and locked stake** — time-based commitment lock that resists balance reduction.

content/pages/stake_weight/index.mdx:33:stake value that scales how strongly that validator's signal counts in Yuma Consensus

content/pages/staking_and_delegation/index.mdx:94:Unstaking and moving stake both change an existing validator support position, but they name
content/pages/staking_and_delegation/index.mdx:95:different outcomes. On an alpha subnet, unstaking withdraws delegated stake and converts subnet
content/pages/staking_and_delegation/index.mdx:97:already held in TAO, so that conversion step does not apply there. Moving stake reassigns support to
content/pages/staking_and_delegation/index.mdx:103:back in unstaked form is describing unstaking. A holder who keeps support committed but attached to
content/pages/staking_and_delegation/index.mdx:104:a different validator is describing moving stake instead.

content/pages/staking_and_delegation/index.mdx:111:[Managing Your Stakes](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/staking-and-delegation/managing-stake-sdk)).

content/pages/staking_and_delegation/index.mdx:138:as describing production stake outcomes on another network.

content/pages/dividends/index.mdx:119:## Distinction from Alpha Staker
content/pages/dividends/index.mdx:121:Dividends and an alpha staker describe the validator-side emission result and a subnet staking
content/pages/dividends/index.mdx:122:position that result flows back toward. Dividends are the validator-side emissions Yuma Consensus
content/pages/dividends/index.mdx:123:produces, which distribution then shares across a validator and the stake supporting it, while an
content/pages/dividends/index.mdx:124:alpha staker holds a subnet's alpha by staking to a validator

content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:2:title: "Transferring Stake"
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:4:  "How transferring stake changes the coldkey that owns a staked position, used when a participant
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:5:  reassigns staked tokens to a different coldkey."
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:8:infoboxTitle: Transferring Stake
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:9:infoboxCaption: Changing coldkey ownership of a staked position.
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:12:    value: Stake management
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:21:# Transferring Stake
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:23:Transferring stake is the operation of changing which coldkey owns a staked position. The
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:25:lists it alongside moving stake and direct unstaking as one of the participant-facing ways to
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:26:rearrange an existing staked position.
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:28:In Taopedia terms, transferring stake names an ownership-change operation. It belongs alongside
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:29:staking (adding stake), unstaking (withdrawing stake), and moving stake (rearranging between
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:30:hotkeys) as one of the core stake-management operations.
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:32:## Why Transferring Stake Exists
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:34:A participant may need to reassign a staked position to a different coldkey — for example, when
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:37:places transferring stake as a participant-facing alternative to unstaking and restaking from the
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:45:stake on a delegated position in a subnet such as netuid 1, that sequence changes how readers should
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:46:interpret evidence about stake transfer mechanics and ownership reassignment outcomes.
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:48:In localnet, stake transfer mechanics can be tested in an isolated environment. Localnet stake
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:52:On testnet, stake transfers can be observed in a shared, non-production network. Testnet stake
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:55:On mainnet, transferring stake is a live Subtensor action that reassigns ownership of delegated
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:56:stake between coldkeys. The
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:61:separates mainnet, testnet, and localnet. A stake transfer example from one environment should not
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:66:Transferring stake is the action of moving a staked position between coldkeys, while toggle transfer
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:71:- **Transferring stake** — the operation that moves stake to another coldkey.
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:74:## Distinction from Effective Stake
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:76:Transferring stake and effective stake separate ownership from validator influence. Transferring
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:77:stake is the operation that changes which coldkey owns a staked position while leaving it on the
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:78:same hotkey, whereas effective stake is the total associated with the validator that position backs,
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:79:so transferring ownership does not move effective stake between validators the way moving stake does
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:80:([Glossary: Effective Stake](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#effective-stake),
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:82:[Glossary: Stake Weight](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#stake-weight)).
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:84:- **Transferring stake** — changing the coldkey that owns a position, same validator.
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:85:- **Effective stake** — the validator total, unmoved when only ownership transfers.
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:89:Transferring stake reassigns coldkey ownership of an existing delegated position. Unstaking
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:90:withdraws stake back to the coldkey, often converting subnet alpha through the pool
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:94:- **Transferring stake** — change ownership while the position stays delegated.
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:95:- **Unstaking** — exit the delegated position and return stake to the coldkey.
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:100:Transferring stake reassigns coldkey ownership over a delegated position that remains staked. The
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:102:lists transferring stake alongside moving stake and direct unstaking as ways to rearrange an
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:103:existing position, but transferring stake specifically changes which coldkey owns the stake rather
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:104:than withdrawing it to an unstaked balance. The validator hotkey receiving the delegation can stay
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:108:Readers should not treat transferring stake as an automatic withdrawal.
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:109:[Unstaking](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#unstaking) returns stake to the
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:110:coldkey as unstaked TAO or converted alpha proceeds; transferring stake moves ownership of the
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:114:## Distinction from Moving Stake
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:116:Moving stake transfers delegated support between hotkeys and/or subnets in one atomic step.
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:117:Transferring stake changes which coldkey owns a delegated position without necessarily changing the
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:119:([Staking and delegation overview: Moving stake](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/staking-and-delegation/delegation#moving-stake),
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:120:[Staking and delegation overview: Transferring stake](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/staking-and-delegation/delegation#transferring-stake)).
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:122:Moving stake re-points delegation. Transferring stake reassigns ownership of the same delegated
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:125:- **Transferring stake** — changes which coldkey owns a delegated position.
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:126:- **Moving stake** — re-points delegated support between hotkeys or subnets.
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:130:Transferring stake and a transfer move different things. Transferring stake reassigns which coldkey
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:131:owns a delegated stake position, while a transfer sends free TAO from one wallet address to another
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:133:[Staking and delegation overview: Transferring stake](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/staking-and-delegation/delegation#transferring-stake)).
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:135:- **Transferring stake** — reassigns ownership of a delegated stake position.
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:140:Transferring stake changes ownership of one staked position between coldkeys. Coldkey swap migrates
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:143:[Staking and delegation overview: Transferring stake](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/staking-and-delegation/delegation#transferring-stake)).
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:145:Use transferring stake when only one delegated position should change owner. Use coldkey swap when
content/pages/transferring_stake/index.mdx:148:- **Transferring stake** — reassigns ownership of one staked position between coldkeys.

+## Validator Take Is Not Stake Weight
+
+Validator take is a distribution split, not a stake-based influence measure. It tells readers what
+share of validator-side emissions or dividends the validator keeps once that validator-side amount
+already exists, before the remainder flows out as [[Delegation Rewards]]
+([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
+[Emission: Distribution](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/emissions#distribution)).
+
+Stake weight vocabulary answers a different question. [[Effective Stake]] and stake weight describe
+how much stake stands behind a validator and how strongly that validator's signal counts in
+consensus, while [[Yuma Consensus]] uses that stake-weighted influence when weights are aggregated
+([Glossary: Effective Stake](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#effective-stake),
+[Glossary: Stake Weight](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#stake-weight),
+[Yuma Consensus](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/yuma-consensus)).
+
+Readers should therefore not treat validator take as a measure of validator influence in consensus.
+Take applies after validator-side emissions or dividends have been produced; stake weight applies
+earlier when validator influence is being counted.
+
 ## What It Represents
 
 Validator take concerns the portion of emissions tied to delegated stake on a selected subnet. On

+## Reader Shortcut
+
+If the question is "who keeps what share of an already-credited validator reward stream," think

+stake weight and [[Effective Stake]]. If the question is "what do delegators receive after the
+validator keeps its configured share," think [[Delegation Rewards]]. If the question is "what
+mechanism turned validator weights into emissions in the first place," think [[Yuma Consensus]].
 
 Validator take should be read as reference vocabulary for emission distribution. It is not a
-recommendation, validator quality score, or complete explanation of staking outcomes
+recommendation, validator quality score, consensus-power score, or complete explanation of staking
+outcomes

 validator-side amount already exists, not the consensus step that produced that amount
 ([Yuma Consensus: Validator emissions](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/yuma-consensus#validator-emissions)).
 
+## Validator Take Is Not Stake Weight
+
+Validator take is a distribution split, not a stake-based influence measure. It tells readers what
+share of validator-side emissions or dividends the validator keeps once that validator-side amount
+already exists, before the remainder flows out as [[Delegation Rewards]]
+([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
+[Emission: Distribution](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/emissions#distribution)).
+
+Stake weight vocabulary answers a different question. [[Effective Stake]] and stake weight describe
+how much stake stands behind a validator and how strongly that validator's signal counts in
+consensus, while [[Yuma Consensus]] uses that stake-weighted influence when weights are aggregated
+([Glossary: Effective Stake](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#effective-stake),
+[Glossary: Stake Weight](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#stake-weight),
+[Yuma Consensus](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/yuma-consensus)).
+
+Readers should therefore not treat validator take as a measure of validator influence in consensus.
+Take applies after validator-side emissions or dividends have been produced; stake weight applies
+earlier when validator influence is being counted.
+
 ## What It Represents
 
 Validator take concerns the portion of emissions tied to delegated stake on a selected subnet. On
@@ -185,12 +204,20 @@
 - **Delegate stake / effective stake** — stake context around a validator.
 - **Validator take** — how the delegated-stake emission share is split at distribution.
 
-## Reader Boundary
+## Reader Shortcut
+
+If the question is "who keeps what share of an already-credited validator reward stream," think
+validator take. If the question is "whose validator signal carries more weight in consensus," think
+stake weight and [[Effective Stake]]. If the question is "what do delegators receive after the
+validator keeps its configured share," think [[Delegation Rewards]]. If the question is "what
+mechanism turned validator weights into emissions in the first place," think [[Yuma Consensus]].
 
 Validator take should be read as reference vocabulary for emission distribution. It is not a
-recommendation, validator quality score, or complete explanation of staking outcomes
+recommendation, validator quality score, consensus-power score, or complete explanation of staking
+outcomes
 ([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
-[Yuma Consensus: Validator emissions](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/yuma-consensus#validator-emissions)).
+[Yuma Consensus: Validator emissions](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/yuma-consensus#validator-emissions),
+[Glossary: Stake Weight](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#stake-weight)).
